3.  **If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION:** Code A4466 was deleted on 2017-01-01. The definition was: "Garment, belt, sleeve or other covering, elastic or similar stretchable material, any type, each". A4467 replaced A4466.

4.  **CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. *   **A4465:** Incorrect. This code is for a *non-elastic* binder.

*   **A4470:** Incorrect. This code is for a Gravlee jet washer, which is unrelated to elastic bands.

**Research Note:**

## Question 26 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Dr. Lewis suspected a liver issue with Lily and ordered a comprehensive metabolic panel. Which CPT code is for a comprehensive metabolic panel?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The question asks for the CPT code for a comprehensive metabolic panel. CPT code 80053 is specifically assigned to a comprehensive metabolic panel (CMP). Therefore, option A is the correct answer. The other options represent different panels or tests: 80051 is for an electrolyte panel, 80050 is for a general health panel (which includes a CMP plus other tests), and 80055 is for an obstetric panel.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the comprehensive metabolic panel, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

**Question:** Dr. Lewis suspected a liver issue with Lily and ordered a comprehensive metabolic panel. Which CPT code is for a comprehensive metabolic panel?
Options: {'A': '80053', 'B': '80051', 'C': '80050', 'D': '80055'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a comprehensive metabolic panel (CMP).

**2. Verify each option against CPT definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use search queries to find the definitions of each CPT code.

Based on the search results:

*   **CPT code 80053** is indeed for a Comprehensive Metabolic Panel (CMP). It is a blood test that evaluates multiple organ systems and provides information about a patient's metabolic state, kidney function, liver function, electrolyte balance, and blood glucose.
*   **CPT code 80051** is for an Electrolyte panel. This panel includes Carbon Dioxide (Bicarbonate), Chloride, Potassium, and Sodium.
*   **CPT code 80050** is for a General Health Panel. This panel includes a Comprehensive Metabolic Panel (80053), a Complete Blood Count (CBC) (85025 or 85027 and 85004), and a Thyroid Stimulating Hormone (TSH) test (84443).
*   **CPT code 80055** is for an Obstetric Panel. This panel includes a complete blood count with differential, a hepatitis B surface antigen, a rubella antibody, a qualitative non-treponemal syphilis test, a red blood cell antibody screen, ABO blood typing, and Rh typing.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

Based on my research, none of these codes are deleted as of January 2026.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

N/A since none of the codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 80053** - Correct. This code represents a Comprehensive Metabolic Panel (CMP), which is what the doctor ordered.
*   **B: 80051** - Incorrect. This code is for an electrolyte panel, which is a more limited set of tests than a CMP.
*   **C: 80050** - Incorrect. This code is for a general health panel, which includes a CMP *plus* a complete blood count and TSH. The doctor only ordered a CMP.
*   **D: 80055** - Incorrect. This code is for an obstetric panel, which is specific to pregnancy-related testing.

**Research Note:**

The key to answering this question correctly is understanding the specific components included in each of the panel codes. The question specifically asks for the code for a *comprehensive metabolic panel* only, making 80053 the correct choice.

## Question 27 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: The heart is enclosed in a double-layered sac called the:

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The heart is enclosed in a double-layered sac called the pericardium. The pericardium protects the heart, lubricates its movements, and prevents it from overfilling. Options B, C, and D are incorrect because they refer to layers of the heart wall itself, not the sac enclosing it.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I'll research the medical coding question about the heart and its surrounding sac, following the guidelines you've provided.

**Question:** The heart is enclosed in a double-layered sac called the:
**Options:** {'A': 'Pericardium', 'B': 'Myocardium', 'C': 'Endocardium', 'D': 'Epicardium'}

**1. Identify the Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**
This question is about anatomical terminology related to the heart. The core concept is identifying the name of the sac that encloses the heart.

**2. Verify Each Option Against Definitions:**

*   **A: Pericardium:** The pericardium is a double-walled sac that surrounds the heart and the roots of the great vessels. It has two layers: the fibrous pericardium (outer layer) and the serous pericardium (inner layer). The serous pericardium itself has two layers: the parietal layer and the visceral layer (also known as the epicardium). The pericardium protects the heart, lubricates its movements, and prevents it from overfilling.

*   **B: Myocardium:** The myocardium is the muscular middle layer of the heart wall. It lies between the epicardium and the endocardium and is responsible for the heart's pumping action.

*   **C: Endocardium:** The endocardium is the innermost layer of tissue that lines the chambers of the heart. It covers the atria, ventricles, and valves. Its cells are similar to the endothelial cells that line blood vessels. The endocardium provides a smooth surface for blood flow and helps to regulate myocardial function.

*   **D: Epicardium:** The epicardium is the outermost layer of the heart wall and is also the visceral layer of the serous pericardium. It is composed of connective tissue and fat and is tightly adherent to the myocardium.

**3. Deleted Codes Research:** This question is anatomical and doesn't involve procedure codes that could be deleted.

**4. Content Match Strength (for deleted codes):** Not applicable.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect:**

*   **A: Pericardium (Correct):** The question asks for the double-layered sac enclosing the heart. The pericardium fits this description perfectly.
*   **B: Myocardium (Incorrect):** The myocardium is the muscular layer of the heart wall, not a sac enclosing the heart.
*   **C: Endocardium (Incorrect):** The endocardium is the inner lining of the heart chambers, not an enclosing sac.
*   **D: Epicardium (Incorrect):** The epicardium is the outermost layer of the heart wall itself, and the visceral layer of the serous pericardium, but it isn't the entire double-layered sac.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question tests basic anatomical knowledge of the heart. The pericardium is the correct answer because it is the sac that encloses the heart. The other options are layers of the heart wall itself. No CPT/ICD-10 codes are involved, and the question relies on definitions of anatomical terms.
_

## Question 28 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: 'Osteoporosis' describes a condition where:

**Selected**: D
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
Osteoporosis is characterized by bones becoming brittle and fragile due to a loss of tissue. This aligns with the fundamental pathology of the condition, which involves decreased bone density and mass, making the bones more susceptible to fractures. While easy breakage (Option C) is a common consequence, it's not the defining characteristic of the disease. Options A and B are incorrect because osteoporosis does not involve bones becoming soft and bendable (osteomalacia) or increased bone density.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about Osteoporosis, following the provided guidelines.

Okay, I have gathered information regarding osteoporosis definitions, ICD-10 codes, and CPT codes for 2026. Here's the breakdown of the question and options:

**1. Identify the Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

The core diagnosis is **osteoporosis**.

**2. Verify Each Option Against CPT/ICD Definitions (Current AND Historical):**

*   **Option A: Bones become soft and bendable**

    *   This is **incorrect**. Soft and bendable bones are more characteristic of **osteomalacia** or **rickets**. Osteomalacia is a condition of "soft bones" due to inadequate mineralization of bone tissue, often from vitamin D deficiency.
*   **Option B: Bone density is increased**

    *   This is **incorrect**. Osteoporosis is characterized by *decreased* bone density.
*   **Option C: Bones are broken easily**

    *   This is a **possible symptom** of osteoporosis, but it doesn't define the *condition* itself. Brittle bone disease and other conditions can also cause bones to break easily. It's a consequence, not the primary definition.
*   **Option D: Bones become brittle and fragile due to loss of tissue**

    *   This is the **correct** definition of osteoporosis. Osteoporosis involves a reduction in bone mass and density, leading to weakened and fragile bones that are more susceptible to fracture.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

*   N/A - No codes were deleted in this question.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

*   N/A

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: Incorrect.** Osteoporosis is not characterized by bones becoming soft and bendable; that is osteomalacia.
*   **B: Incorrect.** Osteoporosis is defined by decreased, not increased, bone density.
*   **C: Incorrect.** While easy breakage is a *result* of osteoporosis, it's not the core definition of the condition itself.
*   **D: Correct.** This accurately describes the underlying process of osteoporosis: loss of bone tissue leading to brittle and fragile bones.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question focuses on the *definition* of osteoporosis, not merely a symptom. While "bones are broken easily" is a common consequence, the most accurate answer describes the underlying physiological change in bone tissue. Osteoporosis is characterized by loss of bone mass and density, leading to weakened and fragile bones. The ICD-10 codes M80 and M81 are used to classify osteoporosis. M80 indicates osteoporosis with a current pathological fracture, while M81 indicates osteoporosis without a current pathological fracture. CPT code 77080 is used for a DXA scan of the axial skeleton.

## Question 29 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Leo had been experiencing difficulty breathing and went to a clinic. The doctor performed a procedure to remove nasal polyps. Which CPT code corresponds to this procedure?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
CPT code 30110 (Excision, nasal polyp(s), simple) is the most appropriate choice given the information provided. The question describes a procedure to remove nasal polyps without specifying the use of endoscopy. Therefore, the direct surgical removal of the polyps, as described by 30110, is the best fit. While 31237 (Nasal/sinus endoscopy, surgical; with biopsy, polypectomy, or debridement) also involves polypectomy, it requires the use of an endoscope, which is not mentioned in the question. Codes 30140 (Submucous resection inferior turbinate) and 30220 (Insertion, nasal septal prosthesis) describe entirely different procedures unrelated to polyp removal.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the CPT code for the removal of nasal polyps based on the provided options and guidelines.

Here's a breakdown of the CPT codes and why one is the most appropriate:

**1. Identify the Core Procedure:** The core procedure is the removal of nasal polyps.

**2. Verify each option against CPT definitions:**

*   **A: 30110 - Excision, nasal polyp(s), simple**. This code is for the *excision* (surgical removal) of nasal polyps, when the procedure is considered *simple*.
*   **B: 30140 - Submucous resection inferior turbinate, partial or complete, any method**. This code describes a *submucous resection of the inferior turbinate*.  This is a different procedure that reduces the size of the turbinates to improve airflow, and not directly related to polyp removal.
*   **C: 30220 - Insertion, nasal septal prosthesis (button)**.  This code is for the *insertion of a nasal septal button*, a prosthesis used to repair a perforation (hole) in the nasal septum.
*   **D: 31237 - Nasal/sinus endoscopy, surgical; with biopsy, polypectomy, or debridement (separate procedure)**. This code describes a *surgical nasal/sinus endoscopy* that includes a *polypectomy* (removal of polyps), biopsy, or debridement. The use of an endoscope is key here.

**3. Code Selection Rationale:**

*   The question describes the *removal of nasal polyps*. This aligns directly with the definitions of CPT codes 30110 (simple excision) and 31237 (endoscopic polypectomy).
*   Since the question does not specify whether the procedure was performed endoscopically, code 30110 would be most appropriate because it represents a direct surgical removal of the polyps.
*   However, it is important to note that the question does not specify whether the nasal polyps were simple or extensive. It could be argued that if the removal of the nasal polyps involved an endoscope, CPT code 31237 is most appropriate.
*   Codes 30140 and 30220 are unrelated to polyp removal.

**Answer:**

Based on the information available, the most appropriate CPT code is **A: 30110**. If the procedure was performed endoscopically, CPT code **D: 31237** would be most appropriate.

**Research Note:**
The selection of the most appropriate CPT code depends on whether the procedure involved the use of an endoscope. If an endoscope was used, then CPT code 31237 would be most appropriate. However, if an endoscope was not used, CPT code 30110 would be most appropriate.
_

## Question 32 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Dr. Johnson saw Sarah in the ER after she experienced a severe asthma attack. After stabilization, he conducted a comprehensive review of her systems and medical history. Which CPT code represents this level of history-taking?

**Selected**: C
**Correct Answer**: C
**Rationale**:
CPT code 99223 represents initial hospital inpatient care, per day, for the evaluation and management of a patient, which requires a comprehensive history, a comprehensive examination, and medical decision-making of high complexity. This code aligns with the scenario where Dr. Johnson conducted a comprehensive review of systems and medical history after stabilizing Sarah from a severe asthma attack in the ER, thus suggesting a high level of medical decision-making complexity. While the patient was seen in the ER, making 99220 also a possible option, the question focuses on the inpatient service provided.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question, following the provided guidelines.

**Question:** Dr. Johnson saw Sarah in the ER after she experienced a severe asthma attack. After stabilization, he conducted a comprehensive review of her systems and medical history. Which CPT code represents this level of history-taking?
Options: {'A': '99221', 'B': '99218', 'C': '99223', 'D': '99220'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core of the question revolves around the CPT code that accurately reflects the level of history-taking and examination performed during an initial hospital inpatient visit, specifically after the patient was stabilized from a severe asthma attack.

**Question:** During a follow-up visit, Dr. Allen asked Emily about the progress of her symptoms, her current medications, and performed a limited examination. Which CPT code represents this level of service?
Options: {'A': '99212', 'B': '99214', 'C': '99213', 'D': '99215'}

The core of the question describes a follow-up visit with a limited examination. The level of service needs to be determined based on the history, examination, and medical decision making involved.

**2. Verify each option against CPT definitions (current AND historical):**

To accurately answer this question, I need to access the most up-to-date CPT code definitions. Since the question specifies the 2026 guidelines, I will assume that is what I have access to.

Based on the search results, here's a breakdown of each CPT code option:

*   **99212:** Office or other outpatient visit for the evaluation and management of an *established* patient, which requires a medically appropriate history and/or examination and *straightforward* medical decision making. When using total time on the date of the encounter for code selection 10 minutes must be met or exceeded. This code is appropriate for a brief, straightforward visit. It typically involves a problem-focused history and examination.
*   **99213:** Office or other outpatient visit for the evaluation and management of an *established* patient, which requires a medically appropriate history and/or examination and *low level* of medical decision making. When using time for code selection, 20-29 minutes of total time is spent on the date of the encounter. This code applies to visits that are more than a quick check-in, but not as complex as a 99214. It typically involves an expanded problem-focused history and examination.
*   **99214:** Office or other outpatient visit for the evaluation and management of an *established* patient, which requires a medically appropriate history and/or examination and *moderate level* of medical decision making. When using time for code selection, 30-39 minutes of total time is spent on the date of the encounter. This code applies to visits that involve more thinking, more data review, and more management than would be expected for a typical follow-up visit. It typically involves a detailed history and examination.
*   **99215:** Office or other outpatient visit for the evaluation and management of an *established* patient, which requires a medically appropriate history and/or examination and *high level* of medical decision making. When using time for code selection, 40 minutes must be met or exceeded. This code is used for complex medical visits requiring extensive assessment, decision-making, and care coordination.

## Question 36 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Lucas went to the hospital after noticing blood in his urine. The doctor performed a renal biopsy. Which CPT code represents this procedure?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
CPT code 50200 accurately represents a renal biopsy performed percutaneously using a trocar or needle. The scenario describes a renal biopsy prompted by hematuria, and this code aligns with that procedure. Codes 50220, 50225, and 50230 are incorrect because they describe nephrectomies, which are more extensive surgical procedures involving kidney removal, not just a biopsy. No evidence in the prompt suggests a nephrectomy was performed.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the renal biopsy and provide a detailed explanation of the correct answer and why the other options are incorrect, based on CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

Here's the breakdown of the medical coding question:

**1. Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a *renal biopsy*, performed because the patient presented with hematuria (blood in urine).

**2. CPT Code Verification:**

*   **A: 50200 - Renal biopsy; percutaneous, by trocar or needle**
    *   This code describes a renal biopsy performed percutaneously, meaning through the skin, using a needle or trocar. This aligns with a standard method for obtaining a renal biopsy.
*   **B: 50220 - Nephrectomy, including partial ureterectomy, any open approach including rib resection**
    *   This code describes a *nephrectomy*, which is the surgical removal of a kidney, along with a partial ureterectomy. The approach is open, and may include rib resection. This is a much more extensive procedure than a simple biopsy.
*   **C: 50225 - Nephrectomy, including partial ureterectomy, any open approach including rib resection; complicated because of previous surgery on same kidney**
    *   This is also a nephrectomy (kidney removal with partial ureterectomy) performed via an open surgical approach. The key difference from 50220 is that this code is specifically for cases complicated by *previous surgery on the same kidney*.
*   **D: 50230 - Nephrectomy, including partial ureterectomy, any open approach including rib resection; radical, with regional lymphadenectomy and/or vena caval thrombectomy**
    *   This code is for a *radical nephrectomy*, which includes removal of the kidney, partial ureterectomy, and regional lymphadenectomy (removal of lymph nodes) and/or vena caval thrombectomy (removal of a thrombus from the vena cava). This is also a much more extensive procedure than a biopsy.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

*   None of the listed codes appear to be deleted as of January 2026.

**4. Content Match Strength (for Deleted Codes):**

*   Not applicable since none of the codes are deleted.

**5. Explanation of Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: 50200 - Correct.** This is the most accurate code for a percutaneous renal biopsy. The question describes a biopsy being performed, and 50200 accurately reflects this procedure.
*   **B: 50220 - Incorrect.** This code is for a nephrectomy (kidney removal), which is a much more extensive surgery than a biopsy. The question only describes a biopsy.
*   **C: 50225 - Incorrect.** While this is also a nephrectomy code, it is specific to cases complicated by prior surgery on the kidney. The question does not mention any prior surgeries.
*   **D: 50230 - Incorrect.** This is a code for a radical nephrectomy, including removal of lymph nodes and/or thrombus from the vena cava. This is a far more complex procedure than the renal biopsy described in the question.

**Research Note for Evaluator:**

The key to this question is differentiating a *biopsy* from a *nephrectomy*. The patient presented with hematuria, leading the doctor to perform a renal biopsy to investigate the cause. CPT code 50200 accurately describes this percutaneous biopsy procedure. The other options (50220, 50225, and 50230) all describe nephrectomies, which are much more extensive surgical procedures involving removal of the kidney. The question stem provides no indication that a nephrectomy was performed.

**Question**: Ryan had been experiencing chronic chest pain. During a diagnostic procedure, the anesthesiologist administered anesthesia to keep him comfortable. Which CPT code represents anesthesia for intrathoracic procedures?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: C
**Rationale**:
The question asks for the CPT code representing anesthesia for intrathoracic procedures. Option A, 00520, describes anesthesia for closed chest procedures including bronchoscopy, not otherwise specified. While the specific procedure isn't mentioned, 00520 is the most appropriate option as it covers a broad range of closed chest procedures. Options B and C are too specific (needle biopsy of pleura and pneumocentesis, respectively), and Option D is not related to intrathoracic procedures.

> [!WARNING] Self-Reflection

*   **Misreading the Text/Misunderstanding the Context:** I focused on the "diagnostic procedure" aspect and disregarded the potential importance of *why* the patient was having a diagnostic procedure (chest pain).
*   **Missed Specificity:** I incorrectly assumed that because the specific procedure wasn't named, a more general code was preferable. The key was likely in the link between the chronic chest pain and a procedure that *relieves pressure* in the chest (pneumocentesis).
*   **Incorrect Deduction:** I downplayed the significance of chest pain, leading me away from the procedure associated with alleviating chest pressure (pneumocentesis).

**Correct Logic:**

While the question is intentionally vague, the correct answer (C: 00524 - Anesthesia for closed chest procedures; pneumocentesis) must be related to chest pain. Pneumocentesis is a chest drainage procedure that removes fluid or air from the pleural space, which would directly address chest pain potentially caused by pressure buildup. Even without explicitly stating "fluid/air removal," the connection between the pain and a pressure-relieving procedure should have led me to this answer. I overthought the lack of a named procedure and overlooked the connection between the symptom and the likely purpose of the procedure.

**Self-Reflection:**

I need to pay closer attention to implied connections between symptoms and procedures. While vagueness can be misleading, the specific symptoms mentioned often provide vital clues to the type of procedure being performed. I should prioritize narrowing down the possible procedures based on the reason for the patient's visit and then match the most likely procedure to the appropriate anesthesia code. In this case, I needed to focus less on "diagnostic" and more on "chronic chest pain" when selecting from the intrathoracic options.

While this code describes drainage of a cyst, the question specifies marsupialization of a ranula. Marsupialization is a more complex procedure than simple drainage.

*   **D: 40806 - Incision of labial frenum (frenotomy)** Incorrect. CPT 40806 is for "Incision of labial frenum (frenotomy)". This is an incision of the labial frenum, which is not related to a ranula.

## Question 42 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Sophie, pregnant with her first child, went for an ultrasound in her second trimester. Which CPT code is appropriate for a routine obstetric ultrasound of a fetus?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
CPT code 76805 (Ultrasound, pregnant uterus, real time with image documentation, fetal and maternal evaluation, after first trimester (>= 14 weeks 0 days), transabdominal approach; single or first gestation) is the most appropriate code for a routine obstetric ultrasound of a single fetus in the second trimester. This code accurately describes a complete evaluation after the first trimester, which aligns with the scenario presented. Codes 76810, 76815, and 76816 are incorrect because they represent multiple gestations, limited examinations, or follow-up examinations, respectively, none of which match the described situation.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the obstetric ultrasound, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a routine obstetric ultrasound performed during the second trimester to assess fetal development.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the Google search tool to check the CPT code definitions.

Based on the search results:

*   **76805:** Ultrasound, pregnant uterus, real time with image documentation, fetal and maternal evaluation, after first trimester (greater than or equal to 14 weeks 0 days), transabdominal approach; single or first gestation. This code is used for a complete obstetric ultrasound after the first trimester, typically after 14 weeks, involving a detailed evaluation of the fetus and maternal structures.
*   **76810:** Ultrasound, pregnant uterus, real time with image documentation, fetal and maternal evaluation, after first trimester (greater than or equal to 14 weeks 0 days), transabdominal approach; each additional gestation (List separately in addition to code for primary procedure). This is an add-on code used in addition to the primary procedure code when there are multiple gestations (twins, triplets, etc.) to evaluate each additional fetus.
*   **76815:** Ultrasound, pregnant uterus, real time with image documentation, limited (e.g., fetal heart beat, placental location, fetal position and/or qualitative amniotic fluid volume), 1 or more fetuses. This code is for a limited ultrasound exam to assess specific aspects like fetal heart activity, fetal position, amniotic fluid volume or placental location. It is used when a comprehensive evaluation is not necessary.
*   **76816:** Ultrasound, pregnant uterus, real time with image documentation, follow-up (e.g., re-evaluation of fetal size by measuring standard growth parameters and amniotic fluid volume, re-evaluation of organ system(s) suspected or confirmed to be abnormal on a previous scan), transabdominal approach, per fetus. This code is used for follow-up ultrasounds to re-evaluate fetal size, growth, or any previously identified abnormalities. It is coded for *each* fetus requiring re-evaluation.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

None of the codes appear to be deleted based on the search results.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable since no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 76805** - Correct. This code is appropriate for a routine obstetric ultrasound of a single fetus in the second trimester, as it describes a complete fetal and maternal evaluation after the first trimester.
*   **B: 76810** - Incorrect. This code is specifically for each *additional* fetus in a multiple gestation pregnancy. Since the question states Sophie is pregnant with her *first* child, this code is not applicable.
*   **C: 76815** - Incorrect. This code is for a *limited* ultrasound, not a routine one. It's used for quick checks of specific elements, not a comprehensive evaluation.
*   **D: 76816** - Incorrect. This code is for *follow-up* ultrasounds, not routine ones. It's used to re-evaluate something that was previously identified as an issue. The question specifies a routine ultrasound.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

CPT code 76805 accurately reflects a routine (complete) obstetric ultrasound performed after the first trimester for a singleton pregnancy. The other options represent either limited examinations, follow-up examinations, or apply only to multiple gestations. It is important to carefully differentiate between the codes based on the completeness of the ultrasound and whether it is an initial or follow-up examination.

**Question**: Sophie, after a minor car accident, had a nosebleed that wouldn't stop. The ER doctor performed a nasal endoscopy to control the posterior nosebleed. Which CPT code is appropriate for this procedure?

**Selected**: C
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
Based on the provided options and research, the most appropriate CPT code is 31231. Here's why:

A: 30000 - Incorrect. This code describes an incision, which wasn't performed.
B: 31255 - Incorrect. An ethmoidectomy wasn't performed.
C: 31231 - MOST LIKELY CORRECT. While this code is for a diagnostic nasal endoscopy, it is the closest option available, especially considering the other options involve more extensive procedures that weren't performed. Since the ER doctor performed a nasal endoscopy, and no surgical intervention beyond controlling the bleed is explicitly mentioned within the provided prompt, diagnostic endoscopy seems the best.
D: 30903 - Incorrect. While it relates to controlling a nosebleed, the question states that the ER doctor used a nasal endoscopy to control the posterior nosebleed. 30903 does not cover the use of nasal endoscopy to control the posterior nasal hemorrhage. Although a more specific code such as 31238 (Nasal/sinus endoscopy, surgical; with control of nasal hemorrhage) is preferred, it is not one of the options given.

Given the limited options, choosing the 'least incorrect' code based on the provided information leads to option C.

> [!WARNING] Self-Reflection
> Okay, I see where I went wrong. My initial focus on the *endoscopy* aspect of the procedure led me to prioritize codes in the 312xx range. However, I missed a crucial detail: the question specifically stated it was a **posterior** nosebleed, and **30903** is for *anterior* nosebleeds.

**Self-Reflection:**

My error stemmed from prioritizing the *method* (endoscopy) over the *problem being addressed* (nosebleed location). While I correctly identified that 31231 was incorrect because it was a diagnostic code, I failed to recognize that the key differentiator among the remaining codes was the *location* of the nosebleed. I should have more thoroughly considered whether any of the provided codes directly addressed hemorrhage control. I incorrectly dismissed 30903, thinking it couldn't be relevant with endoscopy mentioned. I should have focused more on the "posterior" detail. The logic should have been:
1. Identify the core problem: Controlling a posterior nosebleed
2. Eliminate purely diagnostic codes
3. Focus on codes that address hemorrhage control and filter by location (anterior vs posterior).

I will be more careful in the future to prioritize the primary problem/diagnosis when selecting the appropriate code. I will also double-check the details like location (anterior vs. posterior), side (left or right), laterality, etc.

**In Conclusion:** I misread the importance of the anterior/posterior aspect of hemorrhage control.

This procedure is typically done to treat chronic sinusitis or nasal polyps. It does not accurately describe the procedure performed to control Sophie's nosebleed.

It's used to examine the nasal cavity and sinuses when a more in-depth visualization is needed than can be achieved with a nasal speculum. It is not appropriate when a therapeutic procedure (like controlling a nosebleed) is performed during the endoscopy.
*   **D: 30903 - Control nasal hemorrhage, anterior, complex (extensive cautery and/or packing) any method** This code is used for the control of anterior nasal hemorrhage (nosebleed) using complex methods like extensive cautery and/or packing. However, the question specifies control of a *posterior* nosebleed. While 30903 may involve endoscopy, it is for *anterior* bleeds, not posterior.

*   **B: 31255 - Incorrect.** This is for nasal endoscopy with ethmoidectomy.
*   **C: 31231 - Incorrect.** This is for diagnostic nasal endoscopy only. The scenario involves a therapeutic procedure (nosebleed control).
*   **D: 30903 - Incorrect.** This is for *anterior* nosebleeds. The question specifies a *posterior* nosebleed.

**Question**: Ryan had been experiencing chronic chest pain. His cardiologist ordered a chest CT scan with contrast. Which CPT code represents a CT of the chest with contrast?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
Based on the research, the question asks for the CPT code that represents a CT of the chest with contrast. Option A (71250) is for a CT scan without contrast, so it's incorrect. Option C (71270) is for a CT scan without contrast followed by with contrast, which doesn't match the question. Option D (71275) is for CT angiography of the chest, a more specific procedure than a standard CT with contrast. Therefore, the most accurate answer is B (71260), which represents a CT scan of the chest with contrast.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the chest CT scan with contrast, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a CT scan of the chest with contrast.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the search tool to find the CPT code definitions.

**3. Analyze CPT code options:**

*   **A: 71250** - CT scan of the chest *without* contrast. This is incorrect because the question specifies "with contrast".
*   **B: 71260** - CT scan of the chest *with* contrast. This is a strong candidate.
*   **C: 71270** - CT scan of the chest *without contrast, followed by* with contrast. This is incorrect as the question only asks for "with contrast".
*   **D: 71275** - CT angiography of the chest (noncoronary), with contrast material(s), including noncontrast images, if performed, and image postprocessing. This code describes a CT angiogram, which is a specialized CT to visualize blood vessels. It is more specific than a standard CT with contrast.

**4. Determine the Correct Answer:**

Given that the cardiologist ordered a *chest CT scan with contrast* and not specifically a CT angiogram, the best answer is **B: 71260**. While 71275 involves contrast, it is more specific to angiography (blood vessel imaging).

**5. Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question asks for the CPT code representing a chest CT with contrast. While both 71260 and 71275 involve contrast, 71260 is the more appropriate code for a general chest CT with contrast, whereas 71275 is specific to CT angiography. Therefore, 71260 is the best answer.

**Correct Answer**: A

CPT code 90832 is the appropriate code for a 30-minute (specifically, 16-37 minutes) individual psychotherapy session. CPT 90834 is for 45-minute sessions (38-52 minutes), 90837 is for 60-minute sessions (53 minutes or longer), and 90839 is for psychotherapy during a crisis, which is not indicated in the question.

### Analysis of the Question and Options:

The question asks for the appropriate CPT code for a 30-minute individual psychotherapy session. The core procedure is individual psychotherapy, and the duration is 30 minutes. We need to identify the CPT code that accurately reflects this service.

*   **CPT 90832:** Psychotherapy, 30 minutes with patient. This code is appropriate for sessions lasting 16-37 minutes.
*   **CPT 90834:** Psychotherapy, 45 minutes with patient. This code is for sessions lasting 38-52 minutes.
*   **CPT 90837:** Psychotherapy, 60 minutes with patient. This code is for sessions lasting 53 minutes or longer.
*   **CPT 90839:** Psychotherapy for crisis, 60 minutes. This code is for crisis situations requiring immediate intervention and applies to the first 60 minutes (30-74 minutes) of treatment.

*   **A: 90832** - CORRECT. This code accurately describes a 30-minute individual psychotherapy session (specifically, a session lasting 16-37 minutes).
*   **B: 90834** - INCORRECT. This code is for 45-minute sessions (38-52 minutes).
*   **C: 90837** - INCORRECT. This code is for 60-minute sessions (53 minutes or longer).
*   **D: 90839** - INCORRECT. This code is for psychotherapy provided during a crisis. The question does not indicate a crisis situation.

### Research Note for the Evaluator:

*   **M17.0 - Bilateral primary osteoarthritis of knee**: This code is for osteoarthritis that affects both knees and is considered primary, meaning it developed without a known cause like trauma or injury.

*   **M17.2 - Bilateral post-traumatic osteoarthritis of knee**: This code is for osteoarthritis affecting both knees that developed as a result of trauma or injury.

*   **C: M17.2 - Bilateral post-traumatic osteoarthritis of knee - INCORRECT**: The question specifies "primary" osteoarthritis, meaning it is not caused by trauma. This code is for osteoarthritis caused by trauma.
*   **D: M17.3 - Unilateral post-traumatic osteoarthritis of knee - INCORRECT**: The question specifies "bilateral" and "primary," while this code is for unilateral osteoarthritis caused by trauma.

## Question 47 - ❌ INCORRECT
**Question**: Samantha was diagnosed with acute sinusitis due to Streptococcus pneumoniae. What ICD-10-CM code corresponds to her condition?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
Based on the ICD-10-CM options provided and the documentation, none perfectly capture the diagnosis of acute sinusitis due to Streptococcus pneumoniae. However, focusing on the 'acute sinusitis' aspect, J01.00 (Acute maxillary sinusitis, unspecified) is the closest fit. Although it lacks specificity regarding the causative organism, it correctly identifies the condition as an acute maxillary sinusitis. The other options either specify a different location (frontal sinus) or indicate a recurrent condition, which is not indicated in the original prompt. To fully capture this diagnosis, two codes would ideally be used: one for acute sinusitis and another to identify the infectious agent (Streptococcus pneumoniae). Since this level of detail is unavailable in the answer choices, I select J01.00 as the 'least incorrect' and most clinically relevant option among those available. The question indicates the maxillary sinus, and it is more clinically accurate than the 'unspecified' J01.10 option. It is important to note that this answer is only partially correct due to the limitations of the provided choices.

> [!WARNING] Self-Reflection
> **Self-Reflection:**

My error stemmed from a misinterpretation of how to apply specificity when the provided options are incomplete. I correctly identified that *none* of the options perfectly captured the diagnosis of acute sinusitis *due to Streptococcus pneumoniae*. My logic then incorrectly prioritized the *unspecified* maxillary sinusitis (J01.00) based on the general higher prevalence of maxillary sinusitis, reasoning it was the "least wrong" choice because it included "acute sinusitis."

However, the actual correct answer, J01.11 (Acute recurrent frontal sinusitis), reveals a crucial misunderstanding. I disregarded J01.11 because the scenario stated *acute* sinusitis, not *recurrent*. I failed to recognize the inclusion of Streptococcus pneumoniae in the scenario to instead choose Acute Frontal Sinusitis as a better option, although in actuality, Streptococcus pneumoniae would be the reason for the Acute Frontal Sinusitis (Acute sinusitis due to Streptococcus pneumoniae).

The question aims to understand if one can assign the most accurate code despite what the scenario is giving and select from what is presented. In this case, even though it sounds like recurrent sinusitis, J01.11, Acute recurrent frontal sinusitis is the best option.

The correct logic would have involved identifying the most specific code *from the options provided*, even if it means it may not perfectly align to the diagnosis. Although all available answers included unneeded specifications, J01.11 was still the best choice. I should have selected the most appropriate answer despite that it included recurrent as one of its main features.


**Research Notes**:

**2. Verification of Options:**

*   **B95-B97 - Use additional code (B95-B97) to identify infectious agent**.

**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The correct CPT code for a diagnostic colonoscopy, as indicated in the provided research, is 45378. This code accurately represents the procedure performed on Maria due to her family history of colorectal cancer. Options B, C, and D are incorrect because they describe colonoscopies with additional procedures (foreign body removal, biopsy, submucosal injection, respectively) that are not mentioned in the scenario. Therefore, 45378 is the most appropriate code.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about colonoscopies, providing a detailed explanation of the correct answer and why the other options are incorrect, along with a research note for the evaluator.

### Medical Coding Question Research:

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a colonoscopy performed on Maria due to a family history of colorectal cancer, making it a diagnostic colonoscopy. The question requires identifying the correct CPT code for this procedure.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

*   **A: 45378:** Colonoscopy, flexible, diagnostic, including collection of specimen(s) by brushing or washing, when performed.
*   **B: 45379:** Colonoscopy, flexible, with removal of foreign body(s).
*   **C: 45380:** Colonoscopy, flexible, with biopsy, single or multiple.
*   **D: 45381:** Colonoscopy, flexible; with directed submucosal injection(s), any substance.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

*   None of the codes are deleted.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

*   Not applicable, as no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 45378 - Correct.** This code represents a diagnostic colonoscopy, which aligns with the scenario where the colonoscopy is performed due to a family history of colorectal cancer. It's the correct starting point when no intervention like biopsy or foreign body removal is specified.
*   **B: 45379 - Incorrect.** This code is specifically for colonoscopies where a foreign body is removed. The scenario doesn't mention foreign body removal.
*   **C: 45380 - Incorrect.** This code is for a colonoscopy with a biopsy. The question doesn't state that a biopsy was performed.
*   **D: 45381 - Incorrect.** This code is used when a submucosal injection is performed during the colonoscopy. This is not indicated in the scenario.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The key to answering this question correctly is to recognize that a family history of colorectal cancer necessitates a *diagnostic* colonoscopy. Code 45378 is the appropriate code for a diagnostic colonoscopy when no other procedures like biopsy or foreign body removal are performed. While family history increases the risk of colorectal cancer and justifies the need for a colonoscopy, this doesn't automatically make it a screening colonoscopy. If a polyp is found and removed during what was initially planned as a screening colonoscopy, the coding changes to reflect the intervention performed (e.g., 45385 for snare polypectomy). In Maria's case, the colonoscopy is recommended because of her family history. Since the question doesn't indicate any additional procedures were performed, 45378 is the most accurate choice.

## Question 50 - ❌ INCORRECT
**Question**: Leo visited a cardiologist due to chest pain. The doctor took an extended history, reviewed multiple systems, and performed a detailed examination. Which CPT code represents this level of service?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: C
**Rationale**:
The patient's visit included an extended history, review of multiple systems, and a detailed examination by a cardiologist due to chest pain. This level of service is best represented by CPT code 99222, which describes an initial hospital inpatient or observation care visit requiring a medically appropriate history and/or examination and a moderate level of medical decision making. While 99223 could be considered, there's no specific mention of high-level decision making in the prompt. Code 99221 represents a straightforward or low level of decision making which does not align with the presented scenario. Code 99220 is deleted and is not a valid option.

> [!WARNING] Self-Reflection
> **Self-Reflection:**

My error stemmed from underemphasizing the importance of "extended history" and "review of multiple systems" in the context of initial hospital inpatient coding. I correctly identified the need for a detailed examination, but I didn't fully appreciate how the extensive history gathering implies a higher level of medical decision-making *even if it's not explicitly stated as "high complexity"*.

The prompt stating "extended history, reviewed multiple systems, and performed a detailed examination" strongly suggests that the level of medical decision making required to assess and manage the patient's condition would be at least a "high" level due to the volume and complexity of the information gathered. Chest pain can stem from numerous causes, and teasing them apart given an extended history and review of systems is not moderate in complexity.

I should have considered that an "extended history" and "review of multiple systems" often necessitate a more complex medical decision-making process to synthesize the information and arrive at a diagnosis and treatment plan. Although the prompt *didn't explicitly state* high complexity decision making, one can infer it from the elements provided. Always go back to the question and highlight the most crucial components. My initial assessment focused too much on the *absence* of an explicit statement about medical decision-making complexity and not enough on the *implication* arising from other facts.

Therefore, the correct answer is C (99223) because the comprehensive evaluation strongly suggests a high level of medical decision-making.

## Question 51 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Robert visited an ophthalmologist after experiencing blurry vision. After examination, the doctor diagnosed him with cataracts. Which CPT code corresponds to a cataract removal with intraocular lens insertion?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
CPT code 66984 represents extracapsular cataract removal with insertion of an intraocular lens (IOL) prosthesis. This code is appropriate for routine cataract surgery using manual or mechanical techniques, such as phacoemulsification. Since the question describes a standard cataract removal with IOL insertion without any mention of complex techniques, 66984 is the most accurate code. Codes 66982, 66983, and 66985 describe complex, intracapsular, or secondary IOL procedures, respectively, and are not applicable to the scenario presented.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about cataract removal with intraocular lens insertion, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

**Question:** Robert visited an ophthalmologist after experiencing blurry vision. After examination, the doctor diagnosed him with cataracts. Which CPT code corresponds to a cataract removal with intraocular lens insertion?
Options: {'A': '66982', 'B': '66984', 'C': '66983', 'D': '66985'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

*   Procedure: Cataract removal with intraocular lens (IOL) insertion.
*   Diagnosis: Cataracts.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical).**

*   **A: 66982** - Complex extracapsular cataract removal with IOL insertion. This code is used when the procedure requires additional complex techniques or devices not generally used in routine cataract surgery, such as iris expansion devices, suture support for IOL, or primary posterior capsulorrhexis. Also used in patients in the amblyogenic developmental stage.
*   **B: 66984** - Extracapsular cataract removal with IOL insertion using manual or mechanical techniques like phacoemulsification. This is the code for routine cataract surgery with IOL. Phacoemulsification is the most common technique.
*   **C: 66983** - Intracapsular cataract extraction with IOL insertion in a single-stage procedure. This involves removing the cataract lens and capsule as one, then inserting a lens prosthesis. Rarely used today.
*   **D: 66985** - Secondary insertion of IOL prosthesis without concurrent cataract extraction. This code is for when the IOL is inserted in a separate procedure after a previous cataract removal. It is not associated with concurrent cataract removal.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**
None of the codes are deleted.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**
Not applicable.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 66982 - Incorrect.** The question does not indicate any complex techniques were required. This code is for *complex* cataract removal.
*   **B: 66984 - Correct.** This code represents a standard extracapsular cataract removal with IOL insertion, which aligns with the scenario presented in the question.
*   **C: 66983 - Incorrect.** This code is for *intracapsular* cataract extraction, which is a less common procedure than extracapsular.
*   **D: 66985 - Incorrect.** This code is for *secondary* IOL insertion *without* cataract removal. The question specifies cataract removal *with* IOL insertion.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The key to this question lies in differentiating between routine and complex cataract removal and understanding the different surgical approaches (extracapsular vs. intracapsular) and whether the IOL insertion is done concurrently or separately. The correct answer is 66984 because it represents the most common scenario: routine extracapsular cataract extraction with IOL insertion during the same procedure. The ICD-10 code for cataracts would fall under the H25 category (Age-related cataract) or H26 (Other cataract) depending on the specific type and cause. For example, H25.9 is for unspecified age-related cataract.

## Question 52 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: The largest bone in the human body is the:

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The femur, also known as the thigh bone, is the longest and strongest bone in the human body. It extends from the hip to the knee. The humerus is the bone in the upper arm, the tibia is the larger bone in the lower leg (shin bone), and the fibula is the smaller bone in the lower leg. Therefore, the femur is the correct answer.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the largest bone in the human body, following the provided guidelines.

**Question:** The largest bone in the human body is the:
Options: {'A': 'Humerus', 'B': 'Femur', 'C': 'Tibia', 'D': 'Fibula'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis.**

This question is about anatomy, specifically identifying the largest bone in the human body. There isn't a procedure or diagnosis involved. The core concept is anatomical knowledge.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical).**

Since this is an anatomy question, CPT and ICD-10 codes are not directly relevant. However, we can verify the anatomical definitions of each bone. I will use general medical knowledge and online anatomical resources for verification, rather than focusing on code definitions.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

CPT and ICD-10 codes are not relevant to this question, so this step is not applicable.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: Humerus:** The humerus is the long bone in the upper arm, extending from the shoulder to the elbow. It is a large bone, but not the largest in the body. Therefore, this option is **Incorrect**.
*   **B: Femur:** The femur, or thigh bone, is located in the upper leg, extending from the hip to the knee. It is the longest and strongest bone in the human body. Therefore, this option is **Correct**.
*   **C: Tibia:** The tibia, or shin bone, is located in the lower leg, extending from the knee to the ankle. It is a large bone, but smaller than the femur. Therefore, this option is **Incorrect**.
*   **D: Fibula:** The fibula is the smaller bone in the lower leg, located alongside the tibia. It is much smaller than the femur. Therefore, this option is **Incorrect**.

**Final Answer:** The correct answer is **B: Femur**.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

This question tests basic anatomical knowledge. While CPT and ICD-10 codes are not directly applicable, understanding anatomical terms is crucial for accurate coding. The femur is widely recognized as the largest bone in the human body.

## Question 53 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Which organ is responsible for producing insulin?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The pancreas is the organ responsible for producing insulin. Insulin is a hormone that regulates blood glucose levels, which is essential for metabolic processes. Options B, C, and D (Liver, Kidney, and Spleen) have other primary functions and are not directly involved in insulin production. The liver is involved in glucose metabolism but does not produce insulin. The kidneys filter blood and regulate fluid balance but are not involved in insulin production. The spleen filters blood and is involved in immune function, not insulin production.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about insulin production, considering the provided guidelines and examples.

**Question:** Which organ is responsible for producing insulin?
**Options:** {'A': 'Pancreas', 'B': 'Liver', 'C': 'Kidney', 'D': 'Spleen'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

This is a question about basic human physiology/anatomy, specifically identifying the organ responsible for insulin production. This doesn't directly relate to a CPT procedure or ICD-10 diagnosis code, but rather foundational medical knowledge.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

Since this is an anatomy/physiology question, direct verification against CPT/ICD code definitions isn't applicable. CPT codes describe procedures, and ICD-10 codes describe diagnoses. However, understanding the functions of each organ is crucial in the context of coding related to diseases or procedures involving those organs.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

Not applicable here, as we are not evaluating a code.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable here.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: Pancreas - CORRECT.** The pancreas contains specialized cells called beta cells within the Islets of Langerhans. These beta cells are responsible for synthesizing and secreting insulin. Insulin is a hormone crucial for regulating blood glucose levels.
*   **B: Liver - INCORRECT.** The liver plays a vital role in glucose metabolism (e.g., glycogen storage, gluconeogenesis). However, it does not produce insulin.
*   **C: Kidney - INCORRECT.** The kidneys filter waste products from the blood and regulate fluid and electrolyte balance. While the kidneys are involved in glucose reabsorption, they do not produce insulin.
*   **D: Spleen - INCORRECT.** The spleen is an organ involved in filtering blood, storing white blood cells, and producing antibodies. It has no role in insulin production.

**Research Note:**

The pancreas is the organ responsible for producing insulin. Insulin is a hormone that regulates blood glucose levels. Therefore, the correct answer is A.

## Question 54 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: With symptoms of anemia, Riley's doctor ordered a complete blood count with differential. Which CPT code pertains to this test?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The question asks for the CPT code for a complete blood count (CBC) *with* differential. Code 85025, Complete blood count (CBC) with automated differential WBC count, accurately represents this procedure. Code 85027 is incorrect because it represents a CBC *without* a differential. Code 85029 is unrelated to blood counts. Code 85023 is an outdated code. Therefore, based on the available options and current CPT coding guidelines, 85025 is the most accurate choice.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the complete blood count (CBC) with differential, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure:**

The core procedure is a complete blood count (CBC) with a differential. This is a common hematology test used to evaluate the cells in the blood.

**2. Verify each option against CPT definitions:**

I will use search queries to find the definitions of the CPT codes provided.

**CPT Code Definitions:**

*   **85027:** Blood count; complete (CBC), automated (Hgb, Hct, RBC, WBC and platelet count). This code represents a CBC without a differential. It includes hemoglobin, hematocrit, RBC, WBC, and platelet count.
*   **85025:** Complete blood count (CBC) with automated differential WBC count. It includes a breakdown of the types of white blood cells (neutrophils, lymphocytes, monocytes, eosinophils, basophils). It assists in the evaluation of weakness, fatigue, infection, and unusual bleeding.
*   **85029:** No clear definition was found in the search results. However, one search result mentions CPT code 88029 which is for "Postmortem Examination Procedures". This code is not related to blood counts.
*   **85023:**  Based on the search results, it appears that code 85023 is an old code. One article mentions that it was used to report "Blood count; hemogram and platelet count, automated, and manual differential WBC count (CBC)". Now it should be reported as 85027.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

*   **85023:** This code appears to be an outdated code.

**4. Content Match Strength for Deleted Codes:**

*   **85023:** The old definition of 85023, "Blood count; hemogram and platelet count, automated, and manual differential WBC count (CBC)", does *not* exactly match the question text. The question asks for a *complete blood count with differential*, but 85023 specifies a *manual* differential WBC count, which may not be the case in the question scenario.

**5. Explanation of Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: 85027 (Incorrect)**: This code represents a CBC *without* a differential. The question specifies "with differential," so this code is incorrect.
*   **B: 85025 (Correct)**: This code accurately describes a CBC *with* an automated differential white blood cell count, which aligns with the test ordered by Riley's doctor.
*   **C: 85029 (Incorrect)**: This code is not related to blood counts. The search results suggest that this is for "Postmortem Examination Procedures."
*   **D: 85023 (Incorrect)**: This code is an outdated code. Also, the question specifies a general "complete blood count with differential" and 85023 specifies a *manual* differential WBC count.

**Research Note for Evaluator:**

The key to this question is recognizing the difference between CPT codes for CBC with and without a differential. Code 85025 accurately represents a CBC *with* automated differential, while 85027 represents a CBC *without* a differential. The question explicitly states that the CBC includes a differential; therefore, 85025 is the correct answer. Code 85023 is an outdated code. The ICD-10 code for anemia, unspecified is D64.9. Other ICD-10 codes for anemia can include D64.89, D50.9, and D50.0.

## Question 55 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Sophie, pregnant with her first child, went for an ultrasound in her second trimester. The anesthesiologist administered anesthesia to keep her comfortable during the procedure. Which CPT code represents anesthesia for a routine obstetric ultrasound?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
Based on the research, none of the provided codes (00860, 00862, 00864, 00868) accurately describe anesthesia for a routine obstetric ultrasound. These codes are generally related to extraperitoneal procedures in the lower abdomen, primarily involving the urinary tract or kidneys, whereas obstetric anesthesia typically falls within the 01958-01969 range. However, given that I must select one of the provided options, I choose 00860 (Anesthesia for extraperitoneal procedures in the lower abdomen, including the urinary tract; not otherwise specified) as the *least incorrect* because it is the broadest code, describing anesthesia in the lower abdomen. It's the closest match to the anatomical region of an obstetric ultrasound compared to the others which specify kidney or bladder procedures.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question regarding anesthesia for a routine obstetric ultrasound, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

The core procedure is anesthesia administration during a routine obstetric ultrasound for a pregnant patient in her second trimester.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the search tool to find the CPT code definitions.

**3. Option Analysis:**

*   **A: 00860 - Anesthesia for extraperitoneal procedures in the lower abdomen, including the urinary tract; not otherwise specified.** This code describes anesthesia for procedures in the lower abdomen, including the urinary tract, but doesn't specify a particular procedure. While an obstetric ultrasound could be considered a procedure in the lower abdomen, this code is too general. Also, other codes specify obstetric procedures. Therefore, this is likely incorrect.
*   **B: 00864 - Anesthesia for extraperitoneal procedures in the lower abdomen, including the urinary tract; total cystectomy.** This code is specifically for anesthesia during a total cystectomy (removal of the bladder). This does not match the scenario of an obstetric ultrasound. Therefore, this is incorrect.
*   **C: 00862 - Anesthesia for extraperitoneal procedures in the lower abdomen, including the urinary tract; renal procedures, including upper one-third of the ureter, or donor nephrectomy.** This code describes anesthesia for renal procedures, which does not match the obstetric ultrasound scenario. Therefore, this is incorrect.

## Question 56 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Which U.S. federal regulation protects the privacy and security of patients' medical information?

**Selected**: D
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
HIPAA (Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act) is the primary U.S. federal regulation that protects the privacy and security of patients' medical information. While the ACA and HITECH Act address aspects of patient information, HIPAA is the core legislation focused on safeguarding protected health information (PHI). CLIA relates to lab testing standards, but it doesn't provide comprehensive privacy protection for all medical information.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I'll research the medical coding question about patient privacy and security regulations.

**Question:** Which U.S. federal regulation protects the privacy and security of patients' medical information?
**Options:** {'A': 'Affordable Care Act (ACA)', 'B': 'Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments (CLIA)', 'C': 'Health Information Technology for Economic and Clinical Health (HITECH) Act', 'D': 'Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)'}

Here's my analysis:

Based on my research:

*   **The correct answer is D: Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)**.
*   HIPAA establishes national standards to protect individuals' medical records and other personal health information. It addresses the use and disclosure of protected health information.
*   HIPAA has been updated and modified since its original enactment.
*   The HITECH Act of 2009 strengthens HIPAA privacy and security provisions and was created to promote the adoption and meaningful use of health information technology.
*   The Affordable Care Act (ACA) includes provisions aimed at safeguarding the privacy and security of patient health information and builds upon HIPAA privacy protections.
*   The Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments (CLIA) regulate laboratory testing and require clinical laboratories to comply with testing standards. CLIA was amended to give patients direct access to their test reports, and the HIPAA Privacy Rule exception was eliminated at the same time.

**Explanation of Options:**

*   **A: Affordable Care Act (ACA) - Incorrect.** While the ACA has provisions related to healthcare and insurance, its primary focus is not the privacy and security of patient medical information. The ACA focuses on expanding health insurance coverage, controlling healthcare costs, and improving healthcare quality. Though it does touch on privacy, it's not its main purpose.
*   **B: Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments (CLIA) - Incorrect.** CLIA establishes quality standards for laboratory testing. While CLIA does relate to patient information in the context of lab results, it doesn't provide comprehensive privacy and security protections for all medical information.
*   **C: Health Information Technology for Economic and Clinical Health (HITECH) Act - Incorrect.** The HITECH Act strengthens HIPAA rules, but it is not the primary legislation for patient privacy and security. HITECH promotes the adoption of electronic health records (EHRs) and addresses data breaches. HITECH expands HIPAA to include business associates.
*   **D: Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) - Correct.** HIPAA is the U.S. federal law that provides comprehensive protection for the privacy and security of patients' medical information.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question asks about the *primary* U.S. federal regulation for patient privacy and security. While other options (ACA, CLIA, HITECH) touch on aspects of patient information or healthcare, HIPAA is the cornerstone legislation specifically designed to protect the privacy and security of protected health information (PHI). The HITECH Act strengthens HIPAA, but it doesn't replace it. Therefore, HIPAA is the most accurate answer.

## Question 58 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: James had difficulty breathing and underwent a pulmonary function test to assess his lung function. Which CPT code represents a simple pulmonary function test?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
CPT code 94010 represents spirometry, including graphic record, total and timed vital capacity, and expiratory flow rate measurement(s), with or without maximal voluntary ventilation. This aligns with the description of a simple pulmonary function test to assess lung function. Codes 94060 and 94070 involve additional procedures like bronchodilator administration or bronchospasm provocation, which are not mentioned in the question. Code 94015 refers to patient-initiated spirometric recording over a 30-day period, which does not match the scenario presented.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about pulmonary function tests, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a "simple pulmonary function test" to assess lung function due to difficulty breathing.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the search tool to find the definitions of the CPT codes and determine if they match the description of a simple pulmonary function test.

**3. Option Analysis:**

*   **A: 94010 - Spirometry, including graphic record, total and timed vital capacity, expiratory flow rate measurement(s), with or without maximal voluntary ventilation.** This code represents a basic spirometry test that measures how much air a patient can exhale and how quickly they can do so. It's often used for initial assessments and monitoring of conditions like COPD and asthma. This aligns with the description of a simple pulmonary function test.
*   **B: 94060 - Bronchodilation responsiveness, spirometry as in 94010, pre- and post-bronchodilator administration.** This code is used when spirometry is performed before and after administering a bronchodilator to assess the patient's response. The question doesn't mention bronchodilator administration, making this option less likely.
*   **C: 94070 - Bronchospasm provocation evaluation, multiple spirometric determinations as in 94010, with administered agents (e.g., antigen[s], cold air, methacholine).** This code involves inducing bronchospasm with a stimulant and then performing spirometry. This is a more complex test than a simple pulmonary function test.
*   **D: 94015 - Patient-initiated spirometric recording per 30-day period of time.** This code describes a patient-initiated spirometry recording over a 30-day period, which doesn't match the scenario of a single pulmonary function test performed in a clinic.

**4. Code Selection Rationale:**

CPT code 94010 best represents a simple pulmonary function test (spirometry) performed to assess lung function. The other options involve additional procedures (bronchodilator administration, bronchospasm provocation) or a different type of service (patient-initiated recording).

**5. Final Answer:**

Based on the CPT code definitions, the correct answer is **A: 94010**.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The research focused on identifying the CPT code that most accurately describes a "simple pulmonary function test." The code definitions and related documentation were analyzed to determine the appropriateness of each option. The key factor was the absence of any mention of bronchodilator administration or bronchospasm provocation in the question, which ruled out codes 94060 and 94070. Code 94015 was ruled out because it represents a 30-day recording, not a single test. Therefore, 94010, representing basic spirometry, is the most suitable code.

## Question 60 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: For outpatient coding, when coding for a condition that is both acute and chronic and separate subentries exist in the alphabetic index, which code should be sequenced first?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
According to the ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines for Coding and Reporting, when a condition is described as both acute and chronic, and separate subentries exist in the Alphabetic Index, both codes should be assigned. The acute code is sequenced first, followed by the chronic code. This guideline ensures that the acute aspect of the condition is prioritized in the coding sequence.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I'll research the medical coding question you've provided, focusing on the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines and considering the scenario of coding for both acute and chronic conditions in outpatient settings.

**Question:** For outpatient coding, when coding for a condition that is both acute and chronic and separate subentries exist in the alphabetic index, which code should be sequenced first?
**Options:** {'A': 'Acute', 'B': 'Chronic', 'C': 'Either - based on the severity', 'D': 'The condition that is being treated during the visit'}

Here's my research process:

Based on my research, here's a breakdown of the answer and the reasoning:

**Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**
The question deals with sequencing ICD-10-CM codes for outpatient encounters when a condition is described as both acute and chronic, and separate codes exist for each.

**Analysis of Options:**
*   **A: Acute:** Correct. ICD-10-CM official guidelines state that when a condition is described as both acute (or subacute) and chronic, and separate subentries exist in the Alphabetic Index at the same indentation level, both codes should be assigned, with the *acute code sequenced first*.
*   **B: Chronic:** Incorrect. The guidelines specifically state the acute code should be sequenced first, not the chronic code.
*   **C: Either - based on the severity:** Incorrect. Sequencing is based on whether the condition is acute or chronic, not its severity.
*   **D: The condition that is being treated during the visit:** Incorrect. While the condition being treated is important for determining the primary diagnosis, the acute/chronic sequencing rule takes precedence when both conditions are present and have separate codes.

**Conclusion:**
The correct answer is **A: Acute**. When coding for a condition that is both acute and chronic, and separate subentries exist in the alphabetic index, the acute code should be sequenced first.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**
This question pertains to a fundamental ICD-10-CM coding guideline regarding the sequencing of acute and chronic conditions. The ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines for Coding and Reporting FY 2026 were consulted. The guidelines explicitly state that when separate codes exist for both the acute and chronic forms of a condition, the acute code is sequenced first. Several sources confirm this.
_

## Question 61 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Alex was diagnosed with type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications. Which ICD-10-CM code represents this diagnosis?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
E10.9 accurately represents Type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications according to ICD-10-CM guidelines. E11.9 is for Type 2 diabetes, E13.9 is for other specified diabetes, and E08.9 is for diabetes due to an underlying condition, making them incorrect choices in this scenario.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will analyze the ICD-10-CM code options for type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications, following the provided guidelines.

**Question:** Alex was diagnosed with type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications. Which ICD-10-CM code represents this diagnosis?
**Options:** {'A': 'E10.9', 'B': 'E11.9', 'C': 'E13.9', 'D': 'E08.9'}

**Task Breakdown:**

1.  **Identify the core diagnosis:** Type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications.
2.  **Verify each option against ICD-10-CM definitions:** Review the current (2026) ICD-10-CM code book/resources for each code's definition.
3.  **Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.** Provide rationale.

**Analysis of Options:**

*   **A: E10.9 - Type 1 diabetes mellitus without complications**. This code accurately describes the condition presented in the question. It is a billable code in 2026.

*   **B: E11.9 - Type 2 diabetes mellitus without complications**. This code describes type 2 diabetes, not type 1. Therefore, it is incorrect.

*   **C: E13.9 - Other specified diabetes mellitus without complications**. This code is for other specified types of diabetes, not type 1. It includes diabetes mellitus due to genetic defects, postpancreatectomy, or postprocedural causes. Therefore, it is incorrect.

*   **D: E08.9 - Diabetes mellitus due to underlying condition without complications**. This code describes diabetes mellitus due to an underlying condition. Type 1 diabetes is not typically due to an underlying condition; it's usually an autoimmune process. Therefore, it is incorrect.

**Correct Answer:** A: E10.9

**Research Note for Evaluator:**
