*   The core issue is the fitting of a below-the-knee (BK) artificial limb (prosthesis) following an amputation.

**2. HCPCS Level II Code Verification:**

*   **L5631:** *Addition to lower extremity, above knee or knee disarticulation, acrylic socket*. This code describes an *above*-knee prosthesis or knee disarticulation, not a *below*-knee prosthesis.
*   **L5637:** *Addition to lower extremity, below knee, total contact*. This code describes a below-knee prosthesis with total contact.
*   **L5645:** *Addition to lower extremity, below knee, flexible inner socket, external frame*. This code describes a below-knee prosthesis with a flexible inner socket and an external frame.
*   **L5650:** *Additions to lower extremity, total contact, above knee or knee disarticulation socket*. This code is for an *above*-knee or knee disarticulation prosthesis, not a *below*-knee prosthesis.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

*   None of the listed codes appear to be deleted in the 2026 HCPCS Level II code set.

**4. Content Match Strength (for potentially deleted codes):**

*   Not applicable, as none of the codes are deleted.

*   **A: L5631 - Incorrect.** This code is for *above*-knee or knee disarticulation prostheses, not below-knee.
*   **B: L5637 - Potentially Correct.** This code describes a *below-knee* prosthesis with *total contact*. It's a reasonable option if the prosthesis is a total contact type.
*   **C: L5645 - Potentially Correct.** This code describes a *below-knee* prosthesis with a *flexible inner socket and external frame*. This could be the correct option depending on the specific characteristics of the prosthesis.
*   **D: L5650 - Incorrect.** This code is for *above*-knee or knee disarticulation prostheses, not below-knee.

**Recommendation and Research Note:**

Given the information, both L5637 and L5645 could be correct depending on the specific type of below-knee prosthesis fitted. If the prosthesis is a total contact socket, L5637 is the best choice. If it has a flexible inner socket and external frame, L5645 is more accurate. Without further details, it is impossible to definitively select one over the other.

**Research Note for Evaluator:**

The question lacks sufficient detail to pinpoint the *most* accurate code. Both L5637 and L5645 are valid for below-knee prostheses, but differ in socket type (total contact vs. flexible inner socket/external frame). The evaluator should consider whether the question is intentionally ambiguous or if additional information should have been provided.
_

## Question 98 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Tyler had a lump on his thyroid. The endocrinologist performed a fine needle aspiration biopsy. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The question describes a fine needle aspiration (FNA) biopsy of a thyroid lump. While the question specifies "fine needle aspiration," code 60100 technically describes a "percutaneous core needle biopsy." CPT code 60100 (Biopsy thyroid, percutaneous core needle) aligns most closely with the procedure described, even though it is a core needle biopsy, not a fine needle aspiration. According to the research, 60100 applies to any excisional biopsy, regardless of imaging guidance. FNA biopsies are coded differently using codes 10005-10012. Codes 60240, 60220, and 60212 all describe surgical removal of the thyroid gland or portions thereof, which is not what the question describes.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the fine needle aspiration biopsy of the thyroid lump.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a fine needle aspiration (FNA) biopsy of a thyroid lump.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the Google search tool to look up the CPT codes and their descriptions.

Based on the search results:

*   **60100:** Biopsy thyroid, percutaneous core needle. This involves removing a tissue sample from the thyroid gland, typically using a core needle. It's distinct from fine needle aspiration (FNA), which has different codes.
*   **60240:** Thyroidectomy, total or complete. This involves surgical removal of the entire thyroid gland.
*   **60220:** Total thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with or without isthmusectomy. This involves complete surgical removal of one lobe of the thyroid gland, with or without removal of the isthmus.
*   **60212:** Partial thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with contralateral subtotal lobectomy, including isthmusectomy. This involves partial removal of one thyroid lobe, along with subtotal removal of the opposite lobe and the isthmus.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

Based on the search results, none of the codes appear to be deleted. All are active CPT codes.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable since no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 60100 - Correct.** While the question specifies "fine needle aspiration," code 60100 technically describes a "percutaneous core needle biopsy". However,  the search results indicate that 60100 applies to *any* excisional biopsy, regardless of imaging guidance. Also, FNA biopsies are coded differently using codes 10005-10012. Thus, 60100 is the most appropriate answer.
*   **B: 60240 - Incorrect.** This code is for a total thyroidectomy, which is the removal of the entire thyroid gland, not a biopsy.
*   **C: 60220 - Incorrect.** This code is for the removal of an entire thyroid lobe, not a biopsy.
*   **D: 60212 - Incorrect.** This code is for a partial removal of one lobe and a subtotal removal of the other lobe, not a biopsy.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question is slightly ambiguous because it specifies "fine needle aspiration" but the correct answer technically describes a "core needle biopsy." Code 60100 (core needle biopsy) is more appropriate than codes involving partial or total thyroid removal. The search results make it clear that FNA biopsies have their own specific codes (10005-10012) and that 60100 covers any excisional biopsy.

## Question 99 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Lily felt a sudden blockage in her nose. The doctor diagnosed a deviated septum and recommended a septoplasty. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?

**Selected**: D
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
The question describes a septoplasty for a deviated septum. CPT code 30520 specifically describes a septoplasty or submucous resection, with or without cartilage scoring, contouring, or replacement with graft. Codes 31231, 31000, and 31254 describe other nasal or sinus procedures, but not a septoplasty.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the septoplasty procedure, using the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines, and following the instructions you've provided.

**Question:** Lily felt a sudden blockage in her nose. The doctor diagnosed a deviated septum and recommended a septoplasty. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?
Options: {'A': '31231', 'B': '31000', 'C': '31254', 'D': '30520'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis.**

The core procedure is a septoplasty, which is a surgical procedure to correct a deviated septum. The diagnosis is a deviated septum.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical).**

To find the correct CPT code, I will use the following queries.

Based on the search results:

*   **CPT code 31231:** Nasal endoscopy, diagnostic; unilateral or bilateral (separate procedure). This code is for diagnostic purposes, not for a surgical procedure like septoplasty.
*   **CPT code 31000:** Irrigation of the maxillary sinus. This involves flushing out the sinus cavity to clear blockages, which is not the same as a septoplasty.
*   **CPT code 31254:** Nasal/sinus endoscopy with partial ethmoidectomy. This code describes a procedure where an endoscope is used to partially remove the ethmoid sinus tissue, which is different from septoplasty.
*   **CPT code 30520:** Septoplasty or submucous resection, with or without cartilage scoring, contouring or replacement with graft. This code accurately describes the septoplasty procedure mentioned in the question.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

None of the codes appear to be deleted for 2026.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as none of the codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 31231 (Incorrect)**. This code is for a diagnostic nasal endoscopy, not a septoplasty.
*   **B: 31000 (Incorrect)**. This code is for irrigation of the maxillary sinus, not a septoplasty.
*   **C: 31254 (Incorrect)**. This code is for nasal/sinus endoscopy with partial ethmoidectomy, not a septoplasty.
*   **D: 30520 (Correct)**. This code accurately describes a septoplasty or submucous resection.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The correct CPT code for a septoplasty is 30520. The other options represent different procedures involving the nose and sinuses, but they do not specifically describe the repair of a deviated septum. ICD-10 code J34.2 is the correct diagnosis code for a deviated septum.

## Question 100 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Anna received an injection of Botox for her chronic migraines. Which HCPCS Level II code represents the Botox injection?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
J0585 represents the injection of onabotulinumtoxinA, which is the generic name for Botox, aligning with the question's focus on Botox injections for chronic migraines. While other options involve botulinum toxin injections, they pertain to different brand names (Dysport, Myobloc, Xeomin) and thus are not the most accurate choice given the information provided in the question.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about Botox injections for chronic migraines, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is an injection of Botox (botulinum toxin) for the treatment of chronic migraines. This involves administering the medication via injection.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the search tool to find the current definitions of the provided HCPCS Level II codes and any relevant historical information.

**3. Analyze the search results:**

*   **J0585 (Botox):** Injection, onabotulinumtoxinA, 1 unit. This code represents the injection of OnabotulinumtoxinA, with Botox being a brand name.
*   **J0586 (Dysport):** Injection, abobotulinumtoxinA, 5 units. This code represents the injection of AbobotulinumtoxinA, with Dysport being a brand name.
*   **J0587 (Myobloc):** Injection, rimabotulinumtoxinB, 100 units. This code represents the injection of RimabotulinumtoxinB, with Myobloc being a brand name.
*   **J0588 (Xeomin):** Injection, incobotulinumtoxinA, 1 unit. This code represents the injection of IncobotulinumtoxinA, with Xeomin being a brand name.

Botox (OnabotulinumtoxinA) is frequently used in the treatment of chronic migraines.

**4. Determine the Correct Answer and Explain Why:**

The question specifies "Botox" injection. Therefore, the correct answer is:

*   **A: J0585** is the correct code because it represents the injection of onabotulinumtoxinA, which is the generic name for Botox.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect:**

*   **A: J0585 - Correct**. This code accurately describes the injection of onabotulinumtoxinA (Botox).
*   **B: J0586 - Incorrect**. This code represents the injection of abobotulinumtoxinA (Dysport), not Botox.
*   **C: J0587 - Incorrect**. This code represents the injection of rimabotulinumtoxinB (Myobloc), not Botox.
*   **D: J0588 - Incorrect**. This code represents the injection of incobotulinumtoxinA (Xeomin), not Botox.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The key to this question is recognizing that "Botox" is a brand name, and the corresponding HCPCS code (J0585) represents the generic drug, onabotulinumtoxinA. While all the listed codes represent botulinum toxin injections, only J0585 corresponds to the specific drug mentioned in the question. It is also important to verify that the codes are active and relevant for the given year (2026).
